8 | EUROPEAN UNION AGENCY FOR RAILWAYS. SINGLE PROGRAMMING DOCUMENT 2025-2027

--- Document Chunk 337 ---
Foreword

--- Document Chunk 338 ---
Since its creation 20 years ago, ERA has been supporting the European railway stakehold-

--- Document Chunk 339 ---
ers, carrying out an ever-increasing set of crucial tasks for the EU railways. 

--- Document Chunk 340 ---
After ten years of mandate as ERA Executive Director, I am proud of the achievements the 

--- Document Chunk 341 ---
Agency has realised and I remain confident that it will bring even more added value to 

--- Document Chunk 342 ---
the railway sector in the future, especially with the progressive development of the Single 

--- Document Chunk 343 ---
European Railways Area, in line with the political guidelines and priorities expressed 

--- Document Chunk 344 ---
for the new European Commission. 

--- Document Chunk 345 ---
In the recent years, we have witnessed many worrying trends, such as the resurgence of 

--- Document Chunk 346 ---
war on the European continent, certain macroeconomic challenges, as well as increas -

--- Document Chunk 347 ---
ingly serious climate change impacts across the world. In such worrying environment, 

--- Document Chunk 348 ---
transport has a crucial role to play, not only in ensuring the safe transport of people and 

--- Document Chunk 349 ---
goods, but as well in the decarbonisation of the sector and its adaptability to a changing 

--- Document Chunk 350 ---
climate. With only 5 years remaining before the 2030 objectives set in the EC Sustainable 

--- Document Chunk 351 ---
and Smart Mobility Strategy, it will be essential to ensure sustained progress towards the 

--- Document Chunk 352 ---
achievement of the set targets. Safety is also a crucial element for railways, and we need 

--- Document Chunk 353 ---
to ensure the appropriate measures and checks are in place to continuously improve it. “A 

--- Document Chunk 354 ---
sustainable, safe European transport system without frontiers” does therefore not only rep-

--- Document Chunk 355 ---
resent our Agency’s vision statement, but also reflects the ambition the rail sector at large. 

--- Document Chunk 356 ---
In line with its mandate, the European Union Agency for Railways aims at covering a wide 

--- Document Chunk 357 ---
range of areas of work, involving actions to drive the continuation of the progress with 

--- Document Chunk 358 ---
railway safety and interoperability, together with its role of EU-wide authority for Vehicle 

--- Document Chunk 359 ---
Authorisation, Single Safety Certification, and ERTMS Trackside Approval.

--- Document Chunk 360 ---
The multi-annual work programme 2025-2027, together with the annual programme 

--- Document Chunk 361 ---

as well as data and digitalization. As a result, the Agency received an increase of 12 tem -

porary agent posts (TAs) starting in 2023, which should be entirely covered through the

Agency’s existing stream of revenues. The latter represents a significant challenge, espe -

--- Document Chunk 398 ---

--- Document Chunk 400 ---

--- Document Chunk 401 ---

--- Document Chunk 402 ---
In response to the tragic rail accident in Greece in February 2023, with unmeasurable hu -

--- Document Chunk 403 ---
man loss and drastic economic impacts, the Agency has developed a strategic paper with 

--- Document Chunk 404 ---
proposals to enhance the structural response in Europe to avoid such accidents in other 

--- Document Chunk 405 ---
Member States affected by the same weaknesses and failures in their respective national 

--- Document Chunk 406 ---
rail systems. 

--- Document Chunk 407 ---
This strategic paper titled ‘Strengthening Operational Safety (SOS) in Europe’ , endorsed by 

--- Document Chunk 408 ---
the Management in 2023, proposes 2 key initiatives based on a detailed problem analysis, 

--- Document Chunk 409 ---
clear objectives and business requirements, including the estimation of budget and FTEs:

--- Document Chunk 410 ---
  The Priority Countries Programme (PCP), entailing a risk-based approach in 

--- Document Chunk 411 ---
order to identify the key areas of intervention to consistently safeguard and boost 

--- Document Chunk 412 ---
safety levels across the EU Member States;

--- Document Chunk 413 ---
  The Information Sharing System (ISS), as a centralized, pro-active, performing 

--- Document Chunk 414 ---
and technology-proof Information Sharing System for railways in the EU to sup -

--- Document Chunk 415 ---
port the implementation of the CSM ASLP .

--- Document Chunk 416 ---

--- Document Chunk 417 ---
is unfortunately not an associated legal and financial statement. The Agency will continue 

--- Document Chunk 418 ---
to work closely with the EC and with the MSs for unlocking this important stream of work 

--- Document Chunk 419 ---
in the future.

--- Document Chunk 442 ---
Mission statement

--- Document Chunk 443 ---
The vision and mission statements of the Agency (“A sustainable, safe European transport 

--- Document Chunk 444 ---
system without frontiers” and “Moving Europe towards a sustainable and safe railway sys-

--- Document Chunk 445 ---
tem without frontiers” , respectively) were defined in 2021. They reflect its current position 

--- Document Chunk 446 ---
and role, while of course remaining fully in line with the legal mandate of the Agency. 

--- Document Chunk 447 ---
The Agency contributes to the further development and effective functioning of a Single 

--- Document Chunk 448 ---
European Railway Area without frontiers, by guaranteeing a high level of railway safety 

--- Document Chunk 449 ---
and interoperability, while improving the competitive position of the railway sector, as en-

--- Document Chunk 450 ---
visaged by the Agency Regulation 2016/796. In particular, the Agency shall contribute, on 

--- Document Chunk 451 ---
technical matters, to the implementation of Union legislation by developing a common 

--- Document Chunk 452 ---
approach to safety on the Union rail system and by enhancing the level of interoperabil -

--- Document Chunk 453 ---
ity on the Union rail system and associated data, with a specific focus on facilitating the 

--- Document Chunk 454 ---
interoperable deployment of ERTMS and on access to data for pushing rail modernisation 

--- Document Chunk 455 ---
and digitalisation. By working in close cooperation with the national authorities acting in 

--- Document Chunk 456 ---
the fields of railway safety and interoperability, the Agency will substantially contribute 

--- Document Chunk 457 ---
to an increased competitiveness of rail and to the seamless cross-border traffic in the EU. 

--- Document Chunk 458 ---
Moreover, through timely delivery of appropriate regulation that reflects the harmonised 

--- Document Chunk 459 ---
and validated solution proposals from the Europe’s Rail Joint Undertaking, the Agency 

--- Document Chunk 460 ---
contributes significantly to the coordinated and rapid deployment of such solutions, thus 

--- Document Chunk 461 ---
strengthening the competitiveness of rail in the transport mix. All these elements are 

--- Document Chunk 462 ---
translated into rail becoming more attractive and affordable for passengers and freight, 

--- Document Chunk 463 ---
with the Agency playing an active role in supporting the delivery of the European Green 

--- Document Chunk 464 ---
Deal for the EU citizens and businesses.

--- Document Chunk 631 ---
I. General context

--- Document Chunk 632 ---
GENERAL  CONTE xT | 15

--- Document Chunk 633 ---
Transport is an essential part of the European integration, especially given its contribution 

--- Document Chunk 634 ---
to the functioning of the free movement of services, goods, and people. Transport also 

--- Document Chunk 635 ---
represents around 9% of the EU gross added value and directly employs around 11 mil -

--- Document Chunk 636 ---
lion workers, therefore representing an important sector for society at large. EU transport 

--- Document Chunk 637 ---
policies have been developed according to the key principles of safety, sustainability, resil-

--- Document Chunk 638 ---
ience, connectivity, and efficiency.

--- Document Chunk 639 ---
Through its long-term vision for the transport sector and European society, the European 

--- Document Chunk 640 ---
Commission published in 2020 the Sustainable and Smart Mobility Strategy with a de -

--- Document Chunk 641 ---
tailed action plan of 82 initiatives. With this strategy, the Commission presents how the 

--- Document Chunk 642 ---
EU transport system will achieve its needed green and digital transformation and become 

--- Document Chunk 643 ---
more resilient. As outlined in the European Green Deal, the result will be a 90% cut in 

--- Document Chunk 644 ---
carbon emissions by 2050. Regarding the rail sector, the following targets have been set:

--- Document Chunk 645 ---
  Traffic on high-speed rail will double by 2030;

--- Document Chunk 646 ---
  Rail freight traffic will increase by 50% by 2030 and double by 2050;

--- Document Chunk 647 ---
  By 2030, rail and waterborne-based intermodal transport will be able to compete 

--- Document Chunk 648 ---
on equal footing with road-only transport in the EU.

--- Document Chunk 649 ---
The European Union Agency for Railways will support the European Commission, in line 

--- Document Chunk 650 ---
with its accountability ceiling, in achieving these goals, in particular through the further 

--- Document Chunk 651 ---
development and effective functioning of a Single European Railway Area without fron -

--- Document Chunk 652 ---
tiers.

--- Document Chunk 653 ---
The 2025-2027 programming period for the Agency involves two different types of activ-

--- Document Chunk 654 ---
ities: 

--- Document Chunk 655 ---
  The policy tasks contributing to the implementation of Union legislation by devel-

--- Document Chunk 656 ---
oping a common approach to safety on the Union rail system and by enhancing 

--- Document Chunk 657 ---
the level of interoperability on the Union rail system, taking into account the pol -

--- Document Chunk 658 ---
icy priorities identified in the Strengthening Plan and implemented through the 

--- Document Chunk 659 ---
Strengthening Action Plan 2023-2027.

--- Document Chunk 660 ---
  The fully fledged performance of the Agency’s tasks as EU-wide authority for safety 

--- Document Chunk 661 ---
certification, vehicle authorisation and ERTMS trackside approval, along with other 

--- Document Chunk 662 ---
tasks in the field of railway safety and interoperability as foreseen in the Technical 

--- Document Chunk 663 ---
Pillar of the Fourth Railway Package.

--- Document Chunk 664 ---
The Agency continues to implement its work programme following the principles of the 

--- Document Chunk 665 ---
intervention logic, in line with the guidelines provided by the Network of EU Agencies. The 

--- Document Chunk 666 ---
intervention logic supports the Agency by emphasising the desired changes and the road 

--- Document Chunk 667 ---
to its achievement. It is also a thinking process supporting the Agency to design, reconsid-

--- Document Chunk 668 ---
er, and adapt its outputs to the most effective one for a determined outcome. 

--- Document Chunk 669 ---
The Agency also strives to increase its efficiency in delivering the outcomes and impacts 

--- Document Chunk 670 ---
expected by EU citizens. In light of the above, the work programme of the Agency (in its 

--- Document Chunk 671 ---
multi-annual and annual planning) is organised around seven strategic statements, which 

--- Document Chunk 672 ---
project the Agency’s role in relation to its stakeholders, complemented by two transver -

--- Document Chunk 673 ---
sal strategic statements, which capture the Agency’s governance and support functions. 

--- Document Chunk 674 ---
These strategic statements have been in place since the adoption of SPD 2022-2024 and 

--- Document Chunk 675 ---
are extremely important, as they show the direction of travel on which the Agency plans 

--- Document Chunk 676 ---
to embark in order to make railways work better for society, subject of course to its remit 

--- Document Chunk 677 ---
and accountability ceiling.

--- Document Chunk 678 ---
In addition, SPD 2025-2027 will follow and align itself with the actions and resource allo -

--- Document Chunk 679 ---
cations detailed in the Strengthening Action Plan adopted by the MB in November 2022. 

--- Document Chunk 680 ---
The seven priority areas will be highlighted in the annual section and their importance 

--- Document Chunk 681 ---
will be reflected both in terms of FTE and budget allocation. Of course, the Agency will 

--- Document Chunk 682 ---
remain flexible and redeploy resources if needed but this innovative approach provides 

--- Document Chunk 683 ---
a roadmap for all stakeholders regarding the areas on which the Agency will focus in the 

--- Document Chunk 684 ---
coming years. 

--- Document Chunk 685 ---

--- Document Chunk 693 ---

mentation in terms of outputs, resource consumption and revenues, which can allow for 

--- Document Chunk 697 ---

--- Document Chunk 699 ---
grammes instead of 69 projects and services in order to streamline the portfolio adminis -

--- Document Chunk 700 ---
tration and to have a more meaningful and efficient deployment of budget and FTEs, in

A. Struc ture of the multiannual programme 2025-2027

--- Document Chunk 716 ---
The structure of the Agency’s multi-annual work programme is organised according to 9 

--- Document Chunk 717 ---
strategic statements:

--- Document Chunk 718 ---
  Strategic Statement 1 - There will no longer be any technical and operational 

--- Document Chunk 719 ---
barriers to the free movement of people and goods by rail, assets can be reused 

--- Document Chunk 720 ---
throughout Europe. 

--- Document Chunk 721 ---
  Strategic Statement 2 - Rail will become the backbone that supports an envi-

--- Document Chunk 722 ---
ronmentally sustainable multimodal transport system and will be favoured as a 

--- Document Chunk 723 ---
transport mode by the new generations.

--- Document Chunk 724 ---
  Strategic Statement 3 - Rail traffic will become seamless and MaaS (Mobility as 

--- Document Chunk 725 ---
a Service) and LaaS (Logistic as a Service) will be ensured, including multi-leg tick-

--- Document Chunk 726 ---
eting.

--- Document Chunk 727 ---
  Strategic Statement 4 - Rail will be an increasingly safe and secure mode of 

--- Document Chunk 728 ---
transport for its users and workers.

--- Document Chunk 729 ---
  Strategic Statement 5 - Rail will be resilient and agile in responding to emergen-

--- Document Chunk 730 ---
cy situations.

--- Document Chunk 731 ---
  Strategic Statement 6 - Rail will become increasingly economically competitive 

--- Document Chunk 732 ---
as a mode and as a sector.

--- Document Chunk 733 ---
  Strategic Statement 7 - The EU will become the global reference for rail and ERA 

--- Document Chunk 734 ---
authorisations will be globally recognised.

--- Document Chunk 735 ---
  Strategic Statement 8 – The Agency will ensure an effective and efficient gov -

--- Document Chunk 736 ---
ernance of its portfolio of activities in order to offer the best value for money to 

--- Document Chunk 737 ---
citizens and business in the EU

--- Document Chunk 738 ---
  Strategic Statement 9 – The Agency will ensure a performant working environ -

--- Document Chunk 739 ---
ment, based on high quality motivated resources and a collaborative behaviour.

Following guidance from the EU Agencies’ network on the SPD, the Agency proposed for

--- Document Chunk 743 ---
outcome. Given that outcomes are quite difficult to influence directly from outputs, the 

--- Document Chunk 744 ---
concept of intermediate outcomes is interesting given its more direct link with the Agency 

--- Document Chunk 745 ---
and its influence on outcomes.

--- Document Chunk 787 ---
B. C ontent of the multiannual programme 2025-2027

--- Document Chunk 788 ---
For its 2025-2027 work programme, the Agency considers the possible ways of balancing 

--- Document Chunk 789 ---
the demand for its authority work on one hand and the ambition level for the priority areas 

--- Document Chunk 790 ---
detailed in the Strengthening Plan, on the other hand. The authorisations, certificates and 

--- Document Chunk 791 ---
approvals issued by the Agency have a direct impact on the functioning of the rail sector 

--- Document Chunk 792 ---
and bring much added value in terms of safety and interoperability. 

--- Document Chunk 793 ---
Furthermore, should the required additional resources become available, the Agency 

--- Document Chunk 794 ---
would implement, together with Member States, a Priority Country Programme (PCP) 

--- Document Chunk 795 ---
which is a strategic initiative that aims to assess and monitor the state of railway safety and 

--- Document Chunk 796 ---
interoperability legislation implementation in Member States providing a comprehensive 

--- Document Chunk 797 ---
picture of railway safety and helping the MS to identify areas for improvement. In this 

--- Document Chunk 798 ---
perspective, the Agency has additionally developed a robust business case for the devel -

--- Document Chunk 799 ---
opment of a supporting Information Sharing System (ISS), whose objective is to improve 

--- Document Chunk 800 ---
railway safety in the European Union through the sharing and analysis of relevant safety infor-

--- Document Chunk 801 ---
mation, supported by a pro-active, performing and technology-proof system of data exchange.

--- Document Chunk 802 ---
In addition, the strategic role in policy development, research and innovation, and advice 

--- Document Chunk 803 ---
provided by the Agency is recognised as highly important and should continue to be 

--- Document Chunk 804 ---
strengthened. It is equally important to highlight the possible role of the Agency to mon-

--- Document Chunk 805 ---
itor and support the adequate implementation of the existing legal framework through 

--- Document Chunk 806 ---
a harmonised level of maturity both at the levels of operators and national authorities. 

--- Document Chunk 807 ---
To make its operations always more efficient and effective, the Agency will continue to 

--- Document Chunk 808 ---
implement to its full extent the continuous improvement approach to its portfolio and 

--- Document Chunk 809 ---
programme management and make sure that its resources are deployed in those activi -

--- Document Chunk 810 ---
ties where it can have the highest impact and added value for the railway sector and the 

--- Document Chunk 811 ---
EU citizens. The Agency will also continue to develop its workstream on cybersecurity and 

--- Document Chunk 812 ---
will liaise with ENISA to explore future scope for cooperation. Following the cybersecurity 

--- Document Chunk 813 ---
regulation, the Agency will need to increase its resources spent on this item, which is re -

--- Document Chunk 814 ---
flected in the Annual Work Programme.

In the field of Railway Interoperability, the Agency has identified so far six intermediate 

--- Document Chunk 914 ---
outcomes that it can actively influence through its portfolio of TSIs, ERTMS, National rules, 

--- Document Chunk 915 ---
and Registers services. They are essential components, which will lead to the achievement 

--- Document Chunk 916 ---
of the strategic statement. The already identified intermediate outcomes are as follows:

--- Document Chunk 917 ---
1. ERTMS is fully implemented on rolling stock by all Railway Undertakings

--- Document Chunk 918 ---
2. ERTMS is fully implemented on railway infrastructure by all Infrastructure Managers

--- Document Chunk 919 ---
3. All railway rolling stock is TSI compliant by all RUs across the EU. (exc. TAP/TAF & OPE)

--- Document Chunk 920 ---
4. All railway infrastructure is TSI compliant by all IMs across the EU

--- Document Chunk 921 ---
5. National rules (rolling stock & fixed installation) are harmonised across the EU

--- Document Chunk 922 ---
6. All relevant railway-related data is shared in an open and transparent way so that it 

--- Document Chunk 923 ---
is utilisable and useful for the sector

--- Document Chunk 924 ---
Of course, this list will continue to evolve in the future to include additional intermediate 

--- Document Chunk 925 ---
outcomes, as the Agency continues to pursue its full implementation of the intervention 

--- Document Chunk 926 ---
logic. 

--- Document Chunk 927 ---
Following the results of the MB workshop in June 2023 on SPD 2025-2027, where the Man-

--- Document Chunk 928 ---
agement Board expressed its desire for the Agency to propose more knowledge sharing 

--- Document Chunk 929 ---
activities, such as training, and other dissemination activities, the Agency will strengthen 

--- Document Chunk 930 ---
its activities in this domain. Such activities will be coordinated by the ERA Academy, being 

--- Document Chunk 931 ---
the established knowledge sharing vehicle of the Agency. While being part of Strategic 

--- Document Chunk 932 ---
Statement 7, the ERA Academy activities, by their nature, serve all strategic statements of 

--- Document Chunk 933 ---
the Agency.

TSIs & National Technical Rules 

--- Document Chunk 957 ---
The Agency also intends to improve interoperability with, among others: 

--- Document Chunk 958 ---
  TSI development according to the new European Commission requests.

--- Document Chunk 959 ---
  The ERA Change Control Management 

--- Document Chunk 960 ---
  The assessment of notified National Technical Rules (and the drafting of TO in case 

--- Document Chunk 961 ---
of a negative assessment) 

--- Document Chunk 962 ---
  The monitoring of the development of the Ens complementing the TSIs

--- Document Chunk 963 ---

--- Document Chunk 964 ---

--- Document Chunk 965 ---
The stability of the TSIs, together with a successful cleaning up of the remaining national 

--- Document Chunk 966 ---
rules are the foundation of seamless operations across Europe and for an increasing-

--- Document Chunk 967 ---
ly effective authority function, reinforcing the added value of a European mindset in the 

--- Document Chunk 968 ---
EU railway system. 

--- Document Chunk 969 ---
On the 21st of August 2024, The Agency has received from the Commission the EC Request 

--- Document Chunk 970 ---
for recommendations on the multi-annual TSI Revision framework. This request will be the 

--- Document Chunk 971 ---
backbone for the Agency work on the revision of the TSIs with 3 important recommenda-

--- Document Chunk 972 ---
tion milestones: end of 2026, end of 2028 and after 2030. It follows careful consideration 

--- Document Chunk 973 ---
of the Commission’s priorities, the Agency, the stakeholders as well as the EU-Rail Joint 

--- Document Chunk 974 ---
Undertaking and considers 3 main categories: 

--- Document Chunk 975 ---
  The items in the “Completing SERA” category focus on addressing barriers to inter-

--- Document Chunk 976 ---
operability, enhancing safety and increasing efficiency, both in terms of technical 

--- Document Chunk 977 ---
and operational provisions. Another key objective is to achieve deeper harmoni -

--- Document Chunk 978 ---
sation of technical systems, engineering rules and operational rules. This is vital to 

--- Document Chunk 979 ---
ensure these do not create hidden divergences between national systems, and 

--- Document Chunk 980 ---
also to ensure automation of rail processes can target a single system rather than 

--- Document Chunk 981 ---
many variants – thus supporting the vision of truly harmonized rail products for 

--- Document Chunk 982 ---
the SERA. Additionally, actions are being introduced to improve the accessibility 

--- Document Chunk 983 ---
of both railway infrastructure and vehicles for passengers, as well as to support 

--- Document Chunk 984 ---
workplace health and safety of railway workers and to reduce the environmental 

--- Document Chunk 985 ---
impact such as noise.

--- Document Chunk 986 ---
  The majority of “Innovation uptake and future-proof rail” category topics are con -

--- Document Chunk 987 ---
nected to the foreseen outputs of the EU-RAIL JU or contribute to the digitaliza -

--- Document Chunk 988 ---
tion/automation of the railway system to increase its efficiency and improve its at-

--- Document Chunk 989 ---
tractiveness for customers. Special attention is to be paid to the recommendations 

--- Document Chunk 990 ---
to migration and implementation aspects regarding these innovative solutions.

--- Document Chunk 991 ---
  The “Optimised regulation” category aims to improve the coherence, legal reada -

--- Document Chunk 992 ---
bility, certainty, and applicability of the TSIs, as well as to improve and wherever 

--- Document Chunk 993 ---
possible, simplify the testing, assessment, certification and authorisation processes. 

--- Document Chunk 994 ---
In addition to the listed items in this category, further emphasis should be put on the 

--- Document Chunk 995 ---
scope and the structure of TSIs to contribute to the streamlining of the technical frame -

--- Document Chunk 996 ---
work, without impeding the implementation deadlines of already existing legal provisions.

In 2025, the Agency will continue to work on the cleaning-up of national technical and 

--- Document Chunk 1000 ---
safety rules, as well as those on fixed installation and ERTMS. This cleaning-up is an impor-

--- Document Chunk 1001 ---
tant step towards delivering a truly harmonised EU rail system. The Agency will continue 

--- Document Chunk 1002 ---
to focus on the removal of redundant national rules (operational and technical), the har -

--- Document Chunk 1003 ---
monisation of the remaining rules, and the development of AMOCs. 

--- Document Chunk 1004 ---
National Safety Rules & TSI OPE

--- Document Chunk 1005 ---
The Agency will also continue its efforts to harmonise operational rules and practices, with 

--- Document Chunk 1006 ---
the objective of reducing operational barriers for the SERA and improving the overall per-

--- Document Chunk 1007 ---
formance of the railway system, taking into account the interfaces with other EU legis -

--- Document Chunk 1008 ---
lation including ongoing/future developments. The Agency will therefore in the medi -

--- Document Chunk 1009 ---
um-term work on the following items:

--- Document Chunk 1012 ---

Digitalisation & interoperable data

--- Document Chunk 1023 ---
The Agency acknowledges the strategic importance of data and digitalisation in support-

--- Document Chunk 1024 ---
ing a sustainable development of railways in Europe as a competitive mode of transport 

--- Document Chunk 1025 ---
and taking a data centric approach, has the ambition to become a reference for facilitating 

--- Document Chunk 1026 ---
the multi-modal data exchange and queries, based on a common Ontology for railways. 

--- Document Chunk 1027 ---
The Agency has ambitious aims to exploit the potential of digitalization for its operational 

--- Document Chunk 1028 ---
data systems, including a full transformation of the existing registers to support future AI 

--- Document Chunk 1029 ---
and automation capabilities. The Interoperable Data Roadmap will boost the performance 

--- Document Chunk 1030 ---
level of internal processes and will allow to have modern systems such as OSS, Registers, 

--- Document Chunk 1031 ---
etc. fully functioning according to schedule and completely interoperable with commer -

--- Document Chunk 1032 ---
cial software solutions currently adopted by the railway industry to support the operators 

--- Document Chunk 1033 ---
in their daily business. It will also continue to carefully follow the challenges and mitigat -

--- Document Chunk 1034 ---
ing measures associated to both IT security and cybersecurity. 

--- Document Chunk 1035 ---
In 2025 the Agency will continue its work on a CCM process that will control the addition 

--- Document Chunk 1036 ---
of new National Specific Parameters (NSPs) in relation to the Telematics TSIs. In parallel we 

--- Document Chunk 1037 ---
will seek to establish the complete list of current NSPs, use best efforts to start the clean-

--- Document Chunk 1038 ---
up/Validation of current NSPs and propose a timeline for cleaning the list that matches the 

--- Document Chunk 1039 ---
resourcing and priorities of the Agency work progamme. 

--- Document Chunk 1040 ---
For the period 2025-2027, the Agency will still be a top player in ensuring the right frame-

--- Document Chunk 1041 ---
work for the data and information exchange related to assets and services (includ-

--- Document Chunk 1042 ---
ing ticketing data), based on linked data, universal data identifiers and more and better 

--- Document Chunk 1043 ---
data exchanged between operators and customers. This will ensure a seamless exchange 

--- Document Chunk 1044 ---
of data with other modes of transport, thus allowing the customers to benefit from a com-

--- Document Chunk 1045 ---
prehensive logistics chain or the mobility-as-a-service, respectively. 

--- Document Chunk 1046 ---

--- Document Chunk 1048 ---

developed for different purposes, they now appear to be inconsistent between one an -

other in the context of their integration into the European Mobility Data Space (EMDS) for

cy will continue to contribute by facilitating the data exchange for, among various pur -

ERTMS

--- Document Chunk 1081 ---
Seven priorities have been identified: 

--- Document Chunk 1082 ---
a) Future Railway Mobile Communication System (FRMCS): with the upcoming ob -

--- Document Chunk 1083 ---
solescence of GSM-R, the Agency is currently working on this area, which would 

--- Document Chunk 1084 ---
modernise the system from a 2G-based system to a 5G one. By 2027, FRMCS specifi-

--- Document Chunk 1085 ---
cations will be prepared by the EECT RMR. 

--- Document Chunk 1086 ---
b) ETCS and ATO specifications: the Agency would aim at maintaining and improving 

--- Document Chunk 1087 ---
the overall ERTMS specifications by drafting and reviewing the ETCS and ATO speci-

--- Document Chunk 1088 ---
fications within the EECT ETCS. The priorities of new functionalities within this work-

--- Document Chunk 1089 ---
stream are defined within the EC-request for recommendations on the multi-annual 

--- Document Chunk 1090 ---
TSI Revision framework.

In order to achieve the strategic statement 8, the Agency has identified five intermediate 

--- Document Chunk 1524 ---
outcomes that it will actively work towards in the following years through the related 

--- Document Chunk 1525 ---
portfolio of programmes:

--- Document Chunk 1526 ---
1. Staff understand the mission and vision of the Agency, internalise it and have the 

--- Document Chunk 1527 ---
flexibility, the ownership/ autonomy with their activities, and a clear mutual under -

--- Document Chunk 1528 ---
standing of their roles and responsibilities to actively contribute to the strategic di -

--- Document Chunk 1529 ---
rection of the Agency

--- Document Chunk 1530 ---
2. The Agency has a sound and agile governance framework, whose processes and 

--- Document Chunk 1531 ---
administration favour clarity, efficiency and decision making at the right level. 

--- Document Chunk 1532 ---
3. The SPD process steers the Agency’ strategy and multi-annual work programme de-

--- Document Chunk 1533 ---
velopment in an integrated, evidence-based, and coordinated manner as well as 

--- Document Chunk 1534 ---
the monitoring of its effectiveness. This can be achieved through interfacing with 

--- Document Chunk 1535 ---
the internal stakeholders owning the strategies and the external stakeholders (EC, 

--- Document Chunk 1536 ---
EB strategic calendar, etc).

--- Document Chunk 1537 ---
4. SPD is the single reference (for internal and external stakeholders) for all critical tac-

--- Document Chunk 1538 ---
tical information providing the overarching view on the implementation of the pro-

--- Document Chunk 1539 ---
grammes.

--- Document Chunk 1540 ---
5. The Agency is a learning, ethical, legally complying organisation where the deci -

--- Document Chunk 1541 ---
sion-making, the strong financial control, the monitoring and reporting processes 

--- Document Chunk 1542 ---
give the assurance of best value for money.

--- Document Chunk 1543 ---
The other intermediate outcomes will be achieved also through the optimization of the 

--- Document Chunk 1544 ---
ERA planning, monitoring and reporting  capabilities, to enhance the Agency’s pro -

--- Document Chunk 1545 ---
gramme management framework together with the Single Programming Document and 

--- Document Chunk 1546 ---
the Consolidated Annual Activity Report. This will lead to an allocation of resources based 

--- Document Chunk 1547 ---
on impact and intended outcome, fostering the added value created for the railway sector 

--- Document Chunk 1548 ---
and an overall better performance of the Agency. An Action Plan for the Strengthening 

--- Document Chunk 1549 ---
Plan 2023-2027 is put in place, in close link to the SPD implementation and monitoring. 

--- Document Chunk 1550 ---

--- Document Chunk 1551 ---
Agency will continue to invest resources and time to boost and refine the work environ -

--- Document Chunk 1552 ---
ment and cooperation between staff members.

The Agency will also continue to ensure the legal compliance of its activities, outputs,

--- Document Chunk 1555 ---

Clause 4 of the ERA Policy states that “People are our most valuable resource” . Coherently, 

--- Document Chunk 1590 ---
the Agency will implement the new HR strategy 2023-2027, offering clear and transparent 

--- Document Chunk 1591 ---
career paths to staff members, allocate enough resources to make sure that good perfor -

--- Document Chunk 1592 ---
mance and success stories are adequately rewarded, and that skills and competencies are 

--- Document Chunk 1593 ---

--- Document Chunk 1594 ---
but also accompanied by a proper competency management system and communicated 

--- Document Chunk 1595 ---
externally so that interfaces are clear to the stakeholders. The Agency also acknowledges 

--- Document Chunk 1596 ---
the added value of diversity by implementing solutions to improve the gender balance in 

--- Document Chunk 1597 ---
management and operational roles and to widen the number of nationalities employed. 

--- Document Chunk 1598 ---
The Agency will continue further digitalising the HR processes, using to the best extent 

--- Document Chunk 1599 ---
possible European Commission tools, such as SYSPER and MIPS. 

--- Document Chunk 1600 ---
Regarding the IT systems and infrastructure, the Agency aims at moving from digital skills 

--- Document Chunk 1601 ---
of individuals to a more global digital culture. Indeed, while technology supports the 

--- Document Chunk 1602 ---
achievement of various ERA objectives, the IT programmes sees technology as an enabler 

--- Document Chunk 1603 ---
to achieve a “digital as default” value. Of course, this can only be achieved with the support 

--- Document Chunk 1604 ---
of a strong IT security management, information security, and cybersecurity rules to pro -

--- Document Chunk 1605 ---
tect the Agency and its digital assets against cyberthreats. 

--- Document Chunk 1606 ---
In order to achieve these goals, the IT programme will continuously optimise its processes, 

--- Document Chunk 1607 ---
streamline, and automate its workflows to the largest extent possible, while using and pro-

--- Document Chunk 1608 ---
posing digital technologies that have the potential to increase productivity and efficiency 

--- Document Chunk 1609 ---
throughout the Agency. An IT strategy will support these objectives and be followed as 

--- Document Chunk 1610 ---
part of the ERA Strategic Calendar. 

--- Document Chunk 1611 ---
As per the Facility Management Programme, it will continue to ensure that the premises 

--- Document Chunk 1612 ---
currently hosting the headquarters are supporting the business needs, considering the 

--- Document Chunk 1613 ---
aging of the building, as well as the technical installations. It will therefore continue to 

--- Document Chunk 1614 ---
manage and provide specific maintenance through a cycle agreed with the landlord, Va -

--- Document Chunk 1615 ---
lenciennes Métropole. It will also pursue and implement cost-efficient measures to man -

--- Document Chunk 1616 ---
age the building, aiming at reducing the environmental impact of the Agency, including 

--- Document Chunk 1617 ---
but not limited to improving recycling practices, reducing energy and water consump -

--- Document Chunk 1618 ---
tion, and monitoring the quality of services provided by FWC contracts suppliers. 

--- Document Chunk 1619 ---

--- Document Chunk 1620 ---

--- Document Chunk 1863 ---

--- Document Chunk 1864 ---

--- Document Chunk 1865 ---
possible case in order to strengthen the Agency with resources matching the level of 

--- Document Chunk 1866 ---
ambition necessary for achieving the important EC policy objectives for rail, in an effective 

--- Document Chunk 1867 ---

C.5.3. Gro wth of activities at risk of underdelivery 

--- Document Chunk 1940 ---
  In 2025, the Agency anticipates yet another surge of applications, with the highest 

--- Document Chunk 1941 ---
figures ever recorded for VAs and SSCs since the start of the implementation of 

--- Document Chunk 1942 ---
the 4

--- Document Chunk 1943 ---
th Railway Package Technical Pillar. The Agency’s resources have already been 

--- Document Chunk 1944 ---
stretched to the maximum of their capacity in 2024 to cope with the increase of 

--- Document Chunk 1945 ---
F&C activities and there is unfortunately no more room. This issue is also worsened 

--- Document Chunk 1946 ---
by the fact that only a handful of staff have the skills to tackle specific VA with 

--- Document Chunk 1947 ---
ERTMS retrofitting components. Therefore, as the Agency will always prioritise the 

--- Document Chunk 1948 ---
delivery of authority activities, there is a critical risk that the ERTMS objectives for 

--- Document Chunk 1949 ---
2025 will not be achieved due to this intense pressure. Given the expected high 

--- Document Chunk 1950 ---
workload linked to the ERTMS retrofitting, the Agency might even not even be 

--- Document Chunk 1951 ---
able to meet its legal deadlines requirements in this field in 2025. Difficult deci -

--- Document Chunk 1952 ---
sions may have to be taken in 2025 by the Agency if the situation is not resolved.  

--- Document Chunk 1953 ---
The Agency will continue its bilateral discussions with the European Commission 

--- Document Chunk 1954 ---
to assess how to best proceed to tackle this issue. 

--- Document Chunk 1955 ---
  The Agency will also face resource pressure related to the new cybersecurity reg -

--- Document Chunk 1956 ---
ulations (EU 2023/2841) which entered into force on January 7, 2024. The required 

--- Document Chunk 1957 ---
efforts to comply with this legal act are estimated at the moment by the Agency at 

--- Document Chunk 1958 ---
€150,000 per year and 2,3 FTEs. Given the cap on the human resources at the Agen-

--- Document Chunk 1959 ---
cy, and that no additional resources were granted for these activities, the Agency 

--- Document Chunk 1960 ---
will endeavour to perform as well as possible given the current circumstances.

--- Document Chunk 3241 ---
The following general principles guide the application of the legal framework concerning 

--- Document Chunk 3242 ---
the Agency staff:

--- Document Chunk 3243 ---
a)  The core of the Agency staff consists of Temporary Agents. All Temporary Agent 

--- Document Chunk 3244 ---
positions have been identified as long-term positions. Due to the budgetary and 

--- Document Chunk 3245 ---
establishment plan constraints the Agency is obliged to also engage Contract 

--- Document Chunk 3246 ---
Agents in order to fulfil its mission;

--- Document Chunk 3247 ---
b)  Temporary and Contract Agents are treated equivalently as far as possible.

--- Document Chunk 3248 ---
In addition, it should be noted the Agency does not employ officials. However, there are 

--- Document Chunk 3249 ---
cases where EU officials have been engaged following an external selection procedure 

--- Document Chunk 3250 ---
and have therefore acquired the status of Temporary Agent in the Agency (whilst remain-

--- Document Chunk 3251 ---
ing an official on unpaid leave in their institution of origin).

--- Document Chunk 3252 ---
A�2� S election and engagement procedures

--- Document Chunk 3253 ---
The procedure for selection and engagement of Temporary Agents and Contract Agents 

--- Document Chunk 3254 ---
is based on Articles 27-34 of the Staff Regulations and Articles 12-15 and 82-84 of the 

--- Document Chunk 3255 ---
Conditions of Employment of Other  Servants of the European Communities (CEOS) , the 

--- Document Chunk 3256 ---
related Implementing Rules on the engagement and use of Temporary Agents and Con -

--- Document Chunk 3257 ---
tract Agents, the Financial Regulation (European Commission’s Framework and that of the 

--- Document Chunk 3258 ---
Agency), the Code of Good Administrative Behaviour and the data protection rules.

--- Document Chunk 3259 ---
The Agency also makes use of the EPSO CAST lists accessible to Agencies for the engage-

--- Document Chunk 3260 ---
ment of Contract Agents. Because of the Agreement on the European Economic Area 

--- Document Chunk 3261 ---
nationals of Norway, Iceland and Liechtenstein are eligible for working for the Agency.

--- Document Chunk 3262 ---
The selection procedures for the engagement of Temporary Agents are carried out in ac -

--- Document Chunk 3263 ---
cordance with Decision N° 121 of the Administrative Board of the European Railway Agen-

--- Document Chunk 3264 ---
(48) MB Decision n°204 on middle management staff

--- Document Chunk 3265 ---
(49) MB Decision n°203 on types of post and post titles in ERA

--- Document Chunk 3266 ---
(50) MB Decision n°326 on types of posts and post titles

--- Document Chunk 3267 ---

--- Document Chunk 3269 ---
cy laying down the general implementing provisions on the procedure governing the 

--- Document Chunk 3270 ---
engagement and use of temporary staff under Article 2(f ) of the CEOS. 

--- Document Chunk 3271 ---
Depending on the function and the level of tasks and within the limits authorised by the 

--- Document Chunk 3272 ---
establishment plan of the Agency, Temporary Agents are engaged at the following entry 

--- Document Chunk 3273 ---
grades:

--- Document Chunk 3274 ---
  AST 1 to AST 4 for the function group AST

--- Document Chunk 3275 ---
  AD 5 to AD8 for the function group AD

--- Document Chunk 3276 ---
For managerial posts or highly specialised posts, the Agency can engage Temporary 

--- Document Chunk 3277 ---
Agents at grades AD 9 and AD10 or at grade AD12 for Heads of Department. 

--- Document Chunk 3278 ---
The duration of contracts for Temporary Agents is governed by Decision N° ERA-ED-

--- Document Chunk 3279 ---
DEC-1109-2015. Staff holding a long-term post are normally offered an initial contract with 

--- Document Chunk 3280 ---
a duration of four years with the possibility of renewal. The standard practice for a first re-

--- Document Chunk 3281 ---
newal is normally for a two-year period and any further renewal is for an indefinite period. 

--- Document Chunk 3282 ---
For staff on short-term employment, the duration of the contract depends on the dura -

--- Document Chunk 3283 ---
tion of the tasks to be carried out. At ERA, the duration of those contracts is predominantly 

--- Document Chunk 3284 ---
related to the availability and duration of grants, or to a specific time determined activity. 

--- Document Chunk 3285 ---
In very rare cases it is to cover long-term absences.

--- Document Chunk 3286 ---
The Agency is launching the following types of calls, published on ERA website’s Recruit-

--- Document Chunk 3287 ---
ment portal:

--- Document Chunk 3288 ---
  Call for Interest (partial internal re-assignment): CFI/ERA/…

--- Document Chunk 3289 ---
  Internal Mobility for Temporary Agents-Administrators: IM/ERA/AD/…

--- Document Chunk 3290 ---
  Internal Mobility for Temporary Agents-Assistants: IM/ERA/AST/…

--- Document Chunk 3291 ---
  Inter-Agency Mobility for Temporary Agents-Administrators: IAM/ERA/AD/…

--- Document Chunk 3292 ---
  Inter-Agency Mobility for Temporary Agents-Assistants: IAM/ERA/AST/…

--- Document Chunk 3293 ---
  External calls for Temporary Agents-Administrators: ERA/AD/2021/…

--- Document Chunk 3294 ---
  External calls for Temporary Agents-Assistants: ERA/AST/…

--- Document Chunk 3295 ---
  External calls for Contract Agents: ERA/CA/2021/…

--- Document Chunk 3296 ---
A�3� T emporary agents

--- Document Chunk 3297 ---
The ERA Regulation 2016/796 which entered into force in 2016 makes no distinction be -

--- Document Chunk 3298 ---
tween posts for long- term and short-term employment. Still a post can, in accordance 

--- Document Chunk 3299 ---
with Article 16 of Decision N° 121, be defined to be for short-term employment when it 

--- Document Chunk 3300 ---
involves tasks of a limited duration.

--- Document Chunk 3301 ---
The decision to renew contracts of employment of Temporary Agents occupying a long-

--- Document Chunk 3302 ---
term post is taken by the Executive Director based on two considerations: the continuity 

--- Document Chunk 3303 ---
of the post and the competences and performances of the jobholder, in accordance with 

--- Document Chunk 3304 ---
Decision N° ERA-ED-DEC-678-2013 and the Procedure PRO_STA_01 on the “renewal and 

--- Document Chunk 3305 ---
non-renewal of contracts of employment before the expiry date” .

--- Document Chunk 3306 ---
If a TA or former TA is awarded a second contract of employment in the same function 

--- Document Chunk 3307 ---
group, this contract shall be considered as a renewal in the sense of Article 8 of the CEOS if 

--- Document Chunk 3308 ---
the period between the end of the first contract and the starting date of the new contract 

--- Document Chunk 3309 ---
is less than 6 months. If the period between the two contracts of employment is 6 months 

--- Document Chunk 3310 ---
or more or if the new contract is in a different function group, the second contract of em-

--- Document Chunk 3311 ---
ployment shall be considered a new contract of employment.

ANNEx V. HUMAN RESOURCES  2025-2027 – QUALITATIVE | 83

--- Document Chunk 3313 ---
A�4� Contract agents

--- Document Chunk 3314 ---
The selection procedures for the engagement of Contract Agents are carried out in ac -

--- Document Chunk 3315 ---
cordance with Decision n° 210 of the Management Board of the European Union Agency 

--- Document Chunk 3316 ---
on the general provisions for implementing Article 79(2) of the CEOS, governing the con-

--- Document Chunk 3317 ---
ditions of employment of contract staff employed under the terms of Article 3a thereof. 

--- Document Chunk 3318 ---
In accordance with Article 85 of the CEOS, contract staff can be engaged for a fixed pe -

--- Document Chunk 3319 ---
riod of at least three months and not more than five years. Contract Agents are engaged 

--- Document Chunk 3320 ---
for their specific competence in different areas of administration (finance, HR, IT, logistics, 

--- Document Chunk 3321 ---
legal, audit, quality management), in the railway domain or to perform manual or admin -

--- Document Chunk 3322 ---
istrative tasks. 

--- Document Chunk 3323 ---
This type of contract is usually used to meet specific needs such as:

--- Document Chunk 3324 ---
  Administrative tasks;

--- Document Chunk 3325 ---
  Coping with temporary peaks in workloads;

--- Document Chunk 3326 ---
  Launching new activities for which long-term commitment in terms of staffing 

--- Document Chunk 3327 ---
is unclear;

--- Document Chunk 3328 ---
  Replacing staff on long-term absences such as maternity leave, long-term sick 

--- Document Chunk 3329 ---
leave or unpaid leave;

--- Document Chunk 3330 ---
However, increasingly ERA has also engaged Contract Agents for other (long-term) tasks, 

--- Document Chunk 3331 ---
such as:

--- Document Chunk 3332 ---
  Administrative and Logistician Support Agents

--- Document Chunk 3333 ---
  Assistants

--- Document Chunk 3334 ---
  Project Officers

--- Document Chunk 3335 ---
A�5� Seconded National Experts (51)

--- Document Chunk 3336 ---
Seconded National Experts (SNEs) are staff employed by a national, regional or local pub-

--- Document Chunk 3337 ---
lic administration or a public intergovernmental organisation who are seconded to the 

--- Document Chunk 3338 ---
Agency so that it can use their expertise in a particular field. SNEs are seconded from 

--- Document Chunk 3339 ---
their national employer to the Agency’s operational units on the basis of their specific 

--- Document Chunk 3340 ---
competency and technical expertise in the railway domain, based on Decision n° 173 of 

--- Document Chunk 3341 ---
the Management Board of the European Union Agency for Railways laying down rules 

--- Document Chunk 3342 ---
on the secondment to the Agency of seconded national experts and national experts in 

--- Document Chunk 3343 ---
professional training.

--- Document Chunk 3344 ---
A possibility to mandate ‘cost-free’ SNEs also exists, where the Agency does not pay any 

--- Document Chunk 3345 ---
allowances or cover any of the expenses related to the performance of their duties during 

--- Document Chunk 3346 ---
their secondment, although the Agency does not deploy such SNEs at the moment. 

--- Document Chunk 3347 ---
SNEs assist the Agency staff and cannot perform (middle) management duties. The initial 

--- Document Chunk 3348 ---
period of secondment may not be less than six months or more than two years. It 

--- Document Chunk 3349 ---
may be 

--- Document Chunk 3350 ---
renewed once or more up to a total period not exceeding four years. Exceptionally, the 

--- Document Chunk 3351 ---
Agency’s Executive Director may authorise one more extension of the secondment for 

--- Document Chunk 3352 ---
the maximum duration of one year at the end of the four-year period. Each secondment 

--- Document Chunk 3353 ---
and extension are subject to an exchange of letters. An SNE may be seconded once again 

--- Document Chunk 3354 ---
provided that the conditions of secondment still exist and a period of at least six years has 

--- Document Chunk 3355 ---
elapsed between the end of the previous secondment and the new secondment unless 

--- Document Chunk 3356 ---
the previous secondments lasted for less than four years.

--- Document Chunk 3357 ---
(51) SNEs are not employed by the Agency

--- Document Chunk 3358 ---

B� 4 � M obility policy

--- Document Chunk 3471 ---
Mobility within the Agency

--- Document Chunk 3472 ---
Decision N° 121 of the Administrative Board of the European Railway Agency laying down 

--- Document Chunk 3473 ---
the general implementing provisions on the procedure governing the engagement and 

--- Document Chunk 3474 ---
use of temporary staff under Article 2(f ) of the CEOS (adopted on 25.11.2016) and De -

--- Document Chunk 3475 ---
cision n° 210 of the Management Board of the European Union Agency on the general 

--- Document Chunk 3476 ---
provisions for implementing Article 79(2) of the CEOS, governing the conditions of em -

--- Document Chunk 3477 ---
ployment of contract staff employed under the terms of Article 3a thereof enshrine the 

--- Document Chunk 3478 ---
scenarios for internal mobility for TA 2(f ) and CA. 

--- Document Chunk 3479 ---
The Agency considers internal mobility when vacancies arise, but due to the very specific, 

--- Document Chunk 3480 ---
technical competences of a big part of the staff, internal mobility remains limited.

--- Document Chunk 3481 ---
Furthermore, members of the Agency staff can apply for vacant posts within the Agency 

--- Document Chunk 3482 ---
advertised externally. A supplementary agreement in accordance with Article 10 of the 

--- Document Chunk 3483 ---
CEOS will be concluded as required if existing staff get a new job.

--- Document Chunk 3484 ---
Mobility between Union Agencies

--- Document Chunk 3485 ---
The implementing rules on the engagement and use of Temporary Agents 2(f ) and Con-

--- Document Chunk 3486 ---
tract Agents define the scope of mobility between EU Agencies. A very limited number 

--- Document Chunk 3487 ---
of the support staff who have left the Agency in previous years have accepted TA/CA 

--- Document Chunk 3488 ---
positions in other Agencies. 

--- Document Chunk 3489 ---
Increasingly staff members who took up long-term Temporary Agent positions at the 

--- Document Chunk 3490 ---
Agency come from other EU Agencies.

--- Document Chunk 3491 ---
Mobility between the agencies and the institutions

--- Document Chunk 3492 ---
Some posts are filled following an external selection procedure by staff coming from other 

--- Document Chunk 3493 ---
European institutions (in particular the Commission), although the number remains small.

Annex VI. En vironment 

--- Document Chunk 3610 ---
management

--- Document Chunk 3611 ---
A�1� Executive summary

--- Document Chunk 3612 ---
The revised SPD guidelines  (57) require Agencies to compile and formalise their Environ -

--- Document Chunk 3613 ---
ment management policy. To achieve this ambition, the first Environment management 

--- Document Chunk 3614 ---
annex was drafted in which ERA summarised its commitment to higher policy goals, 

--- Document Chunk 3615 ---
the measures already in place, as well as the potential future environment man -

--- Document Chunk 3616 ---
agement initiatives and actions , taking in consideration the responsibilities of the 

--- Document Chunk 3617 ---
Agency as a public administration body, while keeping in mind the impact of environ -

--- Document Chunk 3618 ---
mental initiatives on the Agency’s limited human and financial resources. Despite these 

--- Document Chunk 3619 ---
limitations, the Agency is a socially and environmentally responsible organisation which 

--- Document Chunk 3620 ---
pursues, whenever possible, the adoption and related implementation of environmental 

--- Document Chunk 3621 ---
measures and initiatives that can be achieved with the available means.

--- Document Chunk 3622 ---
The Agency is committed to promote a culture of sustainability acting in a re -

--- Document Chunk 3623 ---
sponsible and sustainable manner  – see point 9 of the European Union Agency for 

--- Document Chunk 3624 ---
Railways Policy (

--- Document Chunk 3625 ---
58). Concern for the environment and promoting a broader sustainability 

--- Document Chunk 3626 ---
agenda are integral to ERA’s professional activities and the management of the organisa-

--- Document Chunk 3627 ---
tion. In addition, the Agency is committed to urgently respond, within the boundaries 

--- Document Chunk 3628 ---
of its mandate and capacity, to the ongoing energy crisis.

--- Document Chunk 3629 ---
The Agency’s aim is to follow and to promote good sustainability practice, to reduce the 

--- Document Chunk 3630 ---
environmental impacts of its activities and to help its stakeholders to do the same. The 

--- Document Chunk 3631 ---
Agency’s existing environment principles   (

--- Document Chunk 3632 ---
59) are covered under the following broader 

--- Document Chunk 3633 ---
topics:

--- Document Chunk 3634 ---
Green building (60) Climate protection Environmental preferable purchasing

--- Document Chunk 3635 ---
Transportation Waste reduction and recycling Sustainable resource management

--- Document Chunk 3636 ---
ERA’s wider work in the railway sector, including its authority and policy contribution to 

--- Document Chunk 3637 ---
a fully-fledged functioning Single European Railway Area, is covered under the 

--- Document Chunk 3638 ---
Annual Work Programme, in particular Strategic Statement 2  (

--- Document Chunk 3639 ---
61) and the specific activity 

--- Document Chunk 3640 ---
“Green agenda” under programme ‘Economic analysis and research’ (ERA1188).

--- Document Chunk 3641 ---
In addition to the broader policy context related to the Green Deal, the Agency pays atten-

--- Document Chunk 3642 ---
tion to the environmental impact of its day-to-day operations (i.e. to its building, staff, 

--- Document Chunk 3643 ---
management, administration, and functioning).

--- Document Chunk 3644 ---
A�2� ER A in the broader policy context related to environment

--- Document Chunk 3645 ---
As an Agency of the European Union, ERA pledges to the Commission’s European 

--- Document Chunk 3646 ---
Green Deal (62) initiative. Consequently, ERA commits to deliver its part of the deal to 

--- Document Chunk 3647 ---
make the EU’s climate, energy, transport and taxation policies fit for reducing net green -

--- Document Chunk 3648 ---
(57) Communication C(2020) 2297 final of 20.4.2020 on the strengthening of the governance of Union Bodies under 

--- Document Chunk 3649 ---
Article 70 of the Financial Regulation 2018/1046 and on the guidelines for the SPD and the CAAR

ANNEx VI. ENVIRONMENT  MANAGEMENT  | 93

--- Document Chunk 3659 ---
house gas emissions by at least 55% by 2030, compared to 1990 levels – as defined in the 

--- Document Chunk 3660 ---
EU Climate Target Plan 2030 (63).

--- Document Chunk 3661 ---
Since the publication of the Communication from the Commission on the European 

--- Document Chunk 3662 ---
Green Deal (64) in December 2019, ERA has strengthened its activities aiming at promoting 

--- Document Chunk 3663 ---
the role of the railways in the decarbonation of the European transport sector. To make the 

--- Document Chunk 3664 ---
European Union the first carbon neutral region in the world by 2050, lowering the trans -

--- Document Chunk 3665 ---
port emissions is crucial. Between 1990 and 2019, the transport emissions have gradually 

--- Document Chunk 3666 ---
increased and reached 25% of the total greenhouse gas emissions of the EU. The transport 

--- Document Chunk 3667 ---
sector is the second sector only to the energy sector in terms of emission.

--- Document Chunk 3668 ---
However, looking at the same period, the emissions of the railway sector have gradually 

--- Document Chunk 3669 ---
decreased and nowadays represent less than 0.5% of the transport-related emissions. In 

--- Document Chunk 3670 ---
addition, railways are also the mode of transport with the lowest external costs (external -

--- Document Chunk 3671 ---
ities). 

--- Document Chunk 3672 ---
ERA has a central role in fostering interoperability and safety of the rail transport which 

--- Document Chunk 3673 ---
should eventually make it more attractive, more efficient and thereby increase the modal 

--- Document Chunk 3674 ---
share of the railways, resulting the greenhouse gas emissions of Europe’s transport sector, 

--- Document Chunk 3675 ---
in line with the objectives of the EC Green Deal:

--- Document Chunk 3676 ---
Figure 2 – Sustainable mobility targets (Source: EC)

ANNEx VI. ENVIRONMENT  MANAGEMENT  | 95

--- Document Chunk 3832 ---
A�3� Environmental impacts of ERA activities 

--- Document Chunk 3833 ---
ERA’s administrative operations related to its building(s) have direct and indirect impacts 

--- Document Chunk 3834 ---
on the environment. ERA’s impact on the environment falls under the following categories:

--- Document Chunk 3835 ---
1.  Use of electricity, including for heating and cooling, water, paper and stationery

--- Document Chunk 3836 ---
2.  Generation of waste and CO2 emissions (including by travelling / commuting)

--- Document Chunk 3837 ---
3. Land use with regards to biodiversity (67)

--- Document Chunk 3838 ---
ERA pays attention to limiting the use of resources, taking the energy crisis into account, 

--- Document Chunk 3839 ---
and minimising negative impacts on the environment.

--- Document Chunk 3840 ---
The recent geopolitical developments make the environmental – and in particular ener -

--- Document Chunk 3841 ---
gy-related issues – more visible than ever before.

--- Document Chunk 3842 ---
A�4� Accountability ceiling of ERA

--- Document Chunk 3843 ---
ERA is committed to do the utmost to advance its environment management and neutral-

--- Document Chunk 3844 ---
ise its impact on the environment. Nevertheless, it needs to be noted that due to outside 

--- Document Chunk 3845 ---
factors ERA’s leverage may be limited regarding some proposed environment actions.

--- Document Chunk 3846 ---
Current ERA headquarters building was put at the disposal of ERA by Valenciennes Métro-

--- Document Chunk 3847 ---
pole through a rental contract. Other buildings (meeting rooms in Lille, parking) used by 

--- Document Chunk 3848 ---
ERA are rented in office buildings and parking lots, where the environment management 

--- Document Chunk 3849 ---
responsibilities and tasks lie with the property owner or manager. In the context of the 

--- Document Chunk 3850 ---
Covid-19 pandemic, the Agency has re-assessed its approach to meetings with stakehold-

--- Document Chunk 3851 ---
ers and has limited the use of office spaces in Lille, as well as the missions of ERA staff and 

--- Document Chunk 3852 ---
externals to Lille headquarters. A large number of the Agency’s meetings have been held 

--- Document Chunk 3853 ---
in remote mode, thus reducing the carbon footprint.

--- Document Chunk 3854 ---
Moreover, ERA’s new headquarters building project has a key focus on environmental 

--- Document Chunk 3855 ---
considerations when setting up specifications and during negotiations. The new building 

--- Document Chunk 3856 ---
project complies with the EMAS/HQE recommendations.

--- Document Chunk 3857 ---
It has to be noted that the railway link with the adjacent Belgian city of Mons is missing for 

--- Document Chunk 3858 ---
decades, with no rail service on the section between Valenciennes and the Franco-Belgian 

--- Document Chunk 3859 ---
border. Despite recent plans brought back the hope for re-establishing the connection, as 

--- Document Chunk 3860 ---
of today this condition leaves no feasible public transportation option for the significant 

--- Document Chunk 3861 ---
proportion of ERA staff living in Belgium. ERA remains a vocal advocate of recommencing 

--- Document Chunk 3862 ---
cross-border railway operations as defined in its Strategic Statement 1  (

--- Document Chunk 3863 ---
68), with a particu-

--- Document Chunk 3864 ---
lar focus on this particular one. Nevertheless as of today, carbon footprint related to staff  

--- Document Chunk 3865 ---
commuting from Belgium to France needs to be mitigated with less desirable alternative 

--- Document Chunk 3866 ---
solutions, such as carpooling.

--- Document Chunk 3867 ---
(67) As per the EMAS regulation (Commission Regulation (EU) 2018/2026 of 19 December 2018 amending Annex IV to 

--- Document Chunk 3868 ---
Regulation (EC) No 1221/2009 on EMAS). Note: the premises have limited urban green space or accessible rooftop 

--- Document Chunk 3869 ---
to be considered for significant improvement of its biodiversity.

--- Document Chunk 3870 ---
(68) “There will no longer be any technical and operational barriers to the free movement of people and goods by rail, 

--- Document Chunk 3871 ---
assets can be reused throughout Europe”

--- Document Chunk 4228 ---

--- Document Chunk 4235 ---

ANNEx Ix. EV ALUATIONS | 107

--- Document Chunk 4409 ---
Terminology

--- Document Chunk 4410 ---
The following terms are used in the SPD – in accordance with the Commission guideline 

--- Document Chunk 4411 ---
on evaluation:

--- Document Chunk 4412 ---
Strategic Statement (77) is a coherent area of action with objectives and resources. It is 

--- Document Chunk 4413 ---
the basic building block for the structure of the annual Work Programme, distinguishing 

--- Document Chunk 4414 ---
between operational activities – directly related to the mission and core tasks of the agen-

--- Document Chunk 4415 ---
cy, and horizontal/ cross-cutting activities – carried out to support operational activities 

--- Document Chunk 4416 ---
and staff.

--- Document Chunk 4417 ---
Objective describes what the agency wants to achieve either in the short or long term.

--- Document Chunk 4418 ---
Indicator is a characteristic or attribute that is measured regularly in order to assess to 

--- Document Chunk 4419 ---
what extent an objective has been met.

--- Document Chunk 4420 ---
Baseline is the point of reference against which achievement or progress towards objec-

--- Document Chunk 4421 ---
tives is measured.

--- Document Chunk 4422 ---
Milestone is an intermediate target set, expressed in quantitative or qualitative terms, 

--- Document Chunk 4423 ---
measuring progress towards the achievement of long-term objectives.

--- Document Chunk 4424 ---
Target is the ultimate desired situation, quantified and timed.

--- Document Chunk 4425 ---
Inputs are the human and financial resources used and the time required to produce 

--- Document Chunk 4426 ---
outputs.

--- Document Chunk 4427 ---
Actions are the work carried out over a certain period of time, consuming resources and 

--- Document Chunk 4428 ---
producing outputs in accordance with the objectives set.

--- Document Chunk 4429 ---
Outputs are what is directly produced or supplied through the agency intervention. They 

--- Document Chunk 4430 ---
often relate to the expected deliverables of the intervention and are identified based on 

--- Document Chunk 4431 ---
its operational objectives.

--- Document Chunk 4432 ---
Outcome is the envisaged medium to long term effects of a programme or policy out -

--- Document Chunk 4433 ---
put. While its results are not easily foreseeable and might not be entirely in the sphere of 

--- Document Chunk 4434 ---
control of the Agency, the outcome represents an intermediate medium-term step be -

--- Document Chunk 4435 ---
tween the agency’ outputs and longer-term societal impacts. The Agency has structured 

--- Document Chunk 4436 ---
its multiannual work programme according to desired outcomes to ensure all of its out -

--- Document Chunk 4437 ---
puts will contribute positively to its vision & ambition.

--- Document Chunk 4438 ---
Results are the direct effects of intervention(s) on the target groups.

--- Document Chunk 4439 ---
Impacts are the indirect or long-term effects of an intervention on the EU or global socie-

--- Document Chunk 4440 ---
ty that are, at least partly, expected to be influenced by agency’s interventions.

--- Document Chunk 4441 ---
(77) R eferred to as “Activity” in former SPDs

Annex x. Strat egy 

--- Document Chunk 4445 ---
for the organisational 

--- Document Chunk 4446 ---
management and 

--- Document Chunk 4447 ---

--- Document Chunk 4448 ---

--- Document Chunk 4449 ---
I. C ontext and background

--- Document Chunk 4450 ---
To fulfil its mandate, the Agency relies on a robust internal control system that ensures 

--- Document Chunk 4451 ---
its operations are efficient, transparent, and aligned with EU Financial Regulations. This 

--- Document Chunk 4452 ---
strategy outlines how Agency’s internal control framework (ICF) supports its mission, en -

--- Document Chunk 4453 ---
sures compliance with financial and regulatory standards, and mitigates risks that could 

--- Document Chunk 4454 ---
jeopardize the achievement of its objectives.

--- Document Chunk 4455 ---
In recent years, the Agency has undergone several key transformations that impacted its 

--- Document Chunk 4456 ---
internal control environment:

--- Document Chunk 4457 ---
  Transition and implementation of the new corporate financial tool for managing 

--- Document Chunk 4458 ---
transactions. The new financial tool allows for better tracking of commitments, 

--- Document Chunk 4459 ---
payments, recovery orders, improving budget management and reducing the like-

--- Document Chunk 4460 ---
lihood of errors. However, the shift to this new system requires strong controls to 

--- Document Chunk 4461 ---
ensure smooth integration, including staff training and system testing to prevent 

--- Document Chunk 4462 ---
disruptions.

--- Document Chunk 4463 ---
  The Agency is a recipient of grants from the European Commission (EC) , 

--- Document Chunk 4464 ---
which are used to fund key projects aimed at improving railway safety and inter -

--- Document Chunk 4465 ---
operability within the EU (including candidate countries). Managing these grants 

--- Document Chunk 4466 ---
requires adherence to strict financial and operational rules, as well as robust inter-

--- Document Chunk 4467 ---
nal controls to ensure that funds are used efficiently and in line with their intended 

--- Document Chunk 4468 ---
purposes. The receipt of grants imposes additional responsibilities on the Agen -

--- Document Chunk 4469 ---
cy to ensure compliance with grant conditions and EU financial rules. Enhanced 

--- Document Chunk 4470 ---
monitoring and reporting mechanisms, particularly through the new IT financial 

--- Document Chunk 4471 ---
tool, will ensure that grant funds are tracked and used effectively. Ex-ante and ex-

--- Document Chunk 4472 ---
post controls will play a crucial role in verifying compliance with grant require -

--- Document Chunk 4473 ---
ments and preventing misuse of funds

--- Document Chunk 4474 ---
  Revision of the Antifraud strategy. Recognising the evolving risks, particularly with 

--- Document Chunk 4475 ---
regards to cyberthreats, the antifraud strategy has been tailored to address the 

--- Document Chunk 4476 ---
Agency’s specific operational environment, which includes regulatory powers 

--- Document Chunk 4477 ---
with significant decision-making authority. It emphasizes the need to protect the 

--- Document Chunk 4478 ---
integrity of its processes, especially in light of the growing reliance on digital sys -

--- Document Chunk 4479 ---
tems and external stakeholders. 

--- Document Chunk 4480 ---
  Gradual introduction of a new strategy/approach for ex-ante and ex-post controls 

--- Document Chunk 4481 ---
considering the above changes. The approach emphasises a risk-based approach 

--- Document Chunk 4482 ---
to control, where high-risk areas receive greater scrutiny. This allows the Agency to 

--- Document Chunk 4483 ---
focus its resources on the most critical areas while ensuring compliance with EU 

--- Document Chunk 4484 ---
Financial Regulations.

--- Document Chunk 4485 ---
ANNEx x. S TRATEGY FOR THE ORGANISATIONAL  MANAGEMENT  AND INTERNAL  CONTROL  SYSTEMS  | 109

--- Document Chunk 4486 ---
II. Objective

--- Document Chunk 4487 ---
The objective of the strategy is to establish and maintain a robust internal control system 

--- Document Chunk 4488 ---
that ensures the effective, efficient, and economical use of resources while safeguarding 

--- Document Chunk 4489 ---
assets and ensuring compliance with the Agency’s mandate and ERA Financial Regula-

--- Document Chunk 4490 ---
tions. This strategy is designed to mitigate risks that could hinder the Agency from achiev-

--- Document Chunk 4491 ---
ing its regulatory and operational objectives, particularly in light of new developments 

--- Document Chunk 4492 ---
such as the introduction of a new IT financial tool, the revised ex-ante and ex-post control 

--- Document Chunk 4493 ---
strategy, and the updated antifraud framework

--- Document Chunk 4494 ---
III. Scope

--- Document Chunk 4495 ---
The strategy covers all financial, operational, and administrative processes within ERA, en-

--- Document Chunk 4496 ---
suring that activities align with ERA financial rules and the Agency’s regulatory framework. 

--- Document Chunk 4497 ---
The scope includes:

--- Document Chunk 4498 ---
  Financial transactions: all financial activities, including the management of grants 

--- Document Chunk 4499 ---
received from the EC, procurement, payments, and budgeting.

--- Document Chunk 4500 ---
  Operational processes: processes related to Agency’s core activities, including pol-

--- Document Chunk 4501 ---
icy and authority tasks, and the integration of new technologies.

--- Document Chunk 4502 ---
  Compliance and risk management: ensuring that the Agency complies with appli-

--- Document Chunk 4503 ---
cable rules and regulations, while effectively managing risks through a combina-

--- Document Chunk 4504 ---
tion of ex-ante and ex-post controls.

--- Document Chunk 4505 ---
  Fraud prevention: addressing potential conflicts of interest, ethical misconduct, 

--- Document Chunk 4506 ---
and cybersecurity risks through the revised antifraud strategy.

--- Document Chunk 4507 ---
While the internal control system is designed to provide reasonable assurance, it cannot 

--- Document Chunk 4508 ---
eliminate all risks due to inherent limitations. These include the complexity of EU regu-

--- Document Chunk 4509 ---
lations, external factors beyond Agency’s control (e.g., economic shifts, political chang -

--- Document Chunk 4510 ---
es), and the reliance on accurate data input from external stakeholders. Additionally, the 

--- Document Chunk 4511 ---
transition to new financial and operational systems requires time for full integration and 

--- Document Chunk 4512 ---
optimization, and temporary inefficiencies may arise during this process. it cannot com -

--- Document Chunk 4513 ---
pletely eliminate the risk of error, fraud, or inefficiency. It is designed to mitigate these risks 

--- Document Chunk 4514 ---
to acceptable levels, considering cost-effectiveness.

--- Document Chunk 4515 ---
IV. K ey actors dealing with internal control

--- Document Chunk 4516 ---
Effective internal control within the Agency is a shared responsibility involving multiple 

--- Document Chunk 4517 ---
key actors:

--- Document Chunk 4518 ---
  Management Board: Represents Member States and institutional stakeholders, 

--- Document Chunk 4519 ---
overseeing internal controls, risk management, and the achievement of strategic 

--- Document Chunk 4520 ---
objectives. It plays a key role in approving budgets and plans, ensuring the overall 

--- Document Chunk 4521 ---
governance of the Agency.

--- Document Chunk 4522 ---
  Executive Director (ED): As the Authorising Officer (AO), the ED is ultimately re -

--- Document Chunk 4523 ---
sponsible for the implementation and functioning of the internal control frame -

--- Document Chunk 4524 ---
work. The ED sets the organizational tone, ensuring that internal controls support 

--- Document Chunk 4525 ---
Agency’s strategic goals and compliance with regulations.

--- Document Chunk 4526 ---
  Heads of Units/Department (AODs) : As Authorising Officers by Delegation 

--- Document Chunk 4527 ---
(AODs), heads of units (HoU) are responsible for ensuring that internal controls are 

--- Document Chunk 4528 ---
effective and efficient in their respective areas. They must monitor risks, implement 

--- Document Chunk 4529 ---
mitigating actions, and ensure adherence to internal control processes.

--- Document Chunk 4530 ---
  Manager of Risk Management and Internal Control : This middle manage -

--- Document Chunk 4531 ---
ment position occupied by the HoU CAP oversees the internal control framework 

--- Document Chunk 4532 ---
110 | EUROPEAN UNION AGENCY FOR RAILWAYS. SINGLE PROGRAMMING DOCUMENT 2025-2027

--- Document Chunk 4533 ---
Multi-annual programming 2025-2027

--- Document Chunk 4534 ---
and risk management processes, ensuring accurate reporting and implementa -

--- Document Chunk 4535 ---
tion of control measures. This role is also key in facilitating the risk management 

--- Document Chunk 4536 ---
process across the Agency.

--- Document Chunk 4537 ---
∑ A ccounting Officer : Certifies the year-end accounts, providing reasonable assurance 

--- Document Chunk 4538 ---
that ERA’s financial records present a true and fair view of the Agency’s financial situation. 

--- Document Chunk 4539 ---
The accounting officer ensures compliance with accounting standards and financial regu-

--- Document Chunk 4540 ---
lations.

--- Document Chunk 4541 ---
∑ I nternal Audit Service (IAS) : Conducts independent assessments of Agency’s internal 

--- Document Chunk 4542 ---
