improvement and ensures compliance with EU regulations.

--- Document Chunk 4544 ---
∑ E uropean Court of Auditors (ECA) : Perform independent audits of ERA’s financial 

--- Document Chunk 4545 ---
transactions and accounts, ensuring legality, regularity, and proper use of funds.

--- Document Chunk 4546 ---
∑ A ll ERA Staff : Responsible for adhering to internal controls within their specific func -

--- Document Chunk 4547 ---
tions. Staff are expected to report any deficiencies or irregularities, ensuring compliance 

--- Document Chunk 4548 ---
with policies and contributing to a culture of integrity.

--- Document Chunk 4549 ---
V. O verview of main controls in place for the five control 

--- Document Chunk 4550 ---
components of the ICF

--- Document Chunk 4551 ---
The ICF is structured around five key components, each supported by specific control 

--- Document Chunk 4552 ---
measures that align with the recent developments in IT, risk management, and fraud pre-

--- Document Chunk 4553 ---
vention.

--- Document Chunk 4554 ---
1. C ontrol Environment:

--- Document Chunk 4555 ---
  Tone at the top: The ED and middle management promote a culture of accounta-

--- Document Chunk 4556 ---
bility, ethical behavior, and transparency. This is reinforced through policies such as 

--- Document Chunk 4557 ---
the Antifraud Strategy and the ethical framework.

--- Document Chunk 4558 ---
  Ethics and Integrity: The updated antifraud strategy focuses on managing conflicts 

--- Document Chunk 4559 ---
of interest and promoting high ethical standards. All staff must submit declarations 

--- Document Chunk 4560 ---
of interests, and mandatory ethics training is provided.

--- Document Chunk 4561 ---
  Organisational structure: Clear lines of responsibility are established, with delega-

--- Document Chunk 4562 ---
tion of powers for executing the budget detailed in internal procedures.

--- Document Chunk 4563 ---
2. R isk Assessment:

--- Document Chunk 4564 ---
The Agency has developed a risk management framework that identifies, assesses, and 

--- Document Chunk 4565 ---
mitigates risks across all areas of its operations. The Agency maintains a corporate risk 

--- Document Chunk 4566 ---
register that is regularly updated to reflect new and emerging risks. Risk management 

--- Document Chunk 4567 ---
processes are embedded within Agency’s operational activities, including financial man -

--- Document Chunk 4568 ---
agement, project implementation, and regulatory oversight.

--- Document Chunk 4569 ---
  Risk Management framework: the Agency conducts risk assessments at the pro -

--- Document Chunk 4570 ---
ject/ service level as well in other specific areas such as IT, sensitive function. Most 

--- Document Chunk 4571 ---
significant risks are recorded in the corporate risk register, assessed both at inher -

--- Document Chunk 4572 ---
ent and residual levels to ensure the effectiveness of controls.

--- Document Chunk 4573 ---
  otrategic and operational risk monitoring: the Manager of Risk Management and 

--- Document Chunk 4574 ---
Internal Control ensures continuous monitoring of risks, focusing on key areas 

--- Document Chunk 4575 ---
such as regulatory compliance and financial management

--- Document Chunk 4576 ---
3. C ontrol Activities:

--- Document Chunk 4577 ---
Control activities are designed to manage risks and ensure compliance with key objec -

--- Document Chunk 4578 ---
tives, including the legality and regularity of transactions, sound financial management, 

--- Document Chunk 4579 ---
fraud prevention, reliability of information, and safeguarding of assets.

--- Document Chunk 4580 ---
ANNEx x. S TRATEGY FOR THE ORGANISATIONAL  MANAGEMENT  AND INTERNAL  CONTROL  SYSTEMS  | 111

--- Document Chunk 4581 ---
  Ex-ante and ex-post controls: the new strategy ensures that preventive measures 

--- Document Chunk 4582 ---
are taken before transactions are finalized (ex-ante) and that compliance and ef-

--- Document Chunk 4583 ---
fectiveness are reviewed after the fact (ex-post).

--- Document Chunk 4584 ---
  Financial Circuits: financial and budget procedures detail steps for implementing 

--- Document Chunk 4585 ---
financial transactions, the roles and responsibilities within financial circuits, and the 

--- Document Chunk 4586 ---
checks to ensure legality and regularity.

--- Document Chunk 4587 ---
  Corrective/Preventive Actions: When systemic issues are identified through ex-

--- Document Chunk 4588 ---
post controls or audits, corrective actions are taken, such as revising procedures 

--- Document Chunk 4589 ---
or retraining staff.

--- Document Chunk 4590 ---
4. I nformation and Communication:

--- Document Chunk 4591 ---
Information related to internal controls, risk management, and financial transactions is 

--- Document Chunk 4592 ---
communicated to relevant staff through regular briefings, training sessions, and internal 

--- Document Chunk 4593 ---
reports:

--- Document Chunk 4594 ---
  Integrated reporting system: A monthly report provides management with up-

--- Document Chunk 4595 ---
to-date information on project progress, budget execution, risks, and corrective 

--- Document Chunk 4596 ---
actions. This system is connected to the new IT financial tool- SUMMA, ensuring 

--- Document Chunk 4597 ---
accurate and real-time data reporting.

--- Document Chunk 4598 ---
  Budgetary status reports: regular budget reports offer a detailed view of budget 

--- Document Chunk 4599 ---
execution by unit and fund source, aiding in performance monitoring and early 

--- Document Chunk 4600 ---
identification of budgetary risks.

--- Document Chunk 4601 ---
  Statement of assurance : The E) is responsible for providing a statement of assur -

--- Document Chunk 4602 ---
ance, ensuring that all information regarding financial management and internal 

--- Document Chunk 4603 ---
control is reliable, comprehensive, and complete. This is supported by reports from 

--- Document Chunk 4604 ---
the internal audit function, risk management assessments, and updates from the 

--- Document Chunk 4605 ---
accounting officer

--- Document Chunk 4606 ---
5. M onitoring Activities:

--- Document Chunk 4607 ---
ERA continuously monitors the implementation of its internal control strategy through 

--- Document Chunk 4608 ---
various mechanisms:

--- Document Chunk 4609 ---
  Audit Results: IAS conducts audits based on a multi-year plan, providing independ-

--- Document Chunk 4610 ---
ent assessments of the internal control system. External audits are performed by 

--- Document Chunk 4611 ---
the ECA and other external bodies, focusing on financial compliance and the le -

--- Document Chunk 4612 ---
gality of transactions.

--- Document Chunk 4613 ---
  Recommendations follow-up: ERA closely monitors the implementation of recom -

--- Document Chunk 4614 ---
mendations from internal and external audits, ensuring that corrective actions are 

--- Document Chunk 4615 ---
completed within agreed deadlines.

--- Document Chunk 4616 ---
  Nonconformity analysis: Instances of nonconformities are analyzed to identify root 

--- Document Chunk 4617 ---
causes and prevent recurrence. Corrective measures are taken as necessary to 

--- Document Chunk 4618 ---
strengthen the control environment.

--- Document Chunk 4619 ---
  ICF assessment: ERA produces an annual assessment report on the effectiveness 

--- Document Chunk 4620 ---
of the ICF. The report is based on control activities, audits, and the outcomes of 

--- Document Chunk 4621 ---
ex-ante and ex-post reviews. All the internal control components and principles 

--- Document Chunk 4622 ---
must be present and functioning well at all levels of the Agency to be considered 

--- Document Chunk 4623 ---
effective. The results of the assessment are reported in the CAAR.

--- Document Chunk 4624 ---
Through this comprehensive strategy, the Agency aims to maintain a high level of trans -

--- Document Chunk 4625 ---
parency and accountability, ensuring that it can continue to meet its objectives while 

--- Document Chunk 4626 ---
safeguarding against financial, operational, and reputational risks.

ANNEx xIV. S TRENGTHENING  AC TION P LAN | 117

--- Document Chunk 4815 ---
Annex xIV. Str engthening 

--- Document Chunk 4816 ---
Action Plan

--- Document Chunk 4817 ---
A�1� Context

--- Document Chunk 4818 ---
In 2022, the Agency’s Management Board adopted the Strengthening Plan prepared by the Agency in close cooperation 

--- Document Chunk 4819 ---
with the European Commission. The purpose of the Strengthening Plan is to make the strongest possible case in order 

--- Document Chunk 4820 ---
to strengthen the Agency with resources matching the level of ambition necessary for achieving the important 

--- Document Chunk 4821 ---
EC policy objectives for rail, in an effective and efficient manner, and benefit from high levels of ambition and 

--- Document Chunk 4822 ---
efficiency within ERA’s structure and methods.

--- Document Chunk 4823 ---
With the document serving as a basis for the internal EC budget negotiations in 2022, the Agency received a proposed 

--- Document Chunk 4824 ---
increase of 12 TAs in 2022. While the additional TA allocation is lower compared to the request from the Strengthening 

--- Document Chunk 4825 ---
Plan (12 TAs proposed out of the 22 TAs requested), it can offer a good basis for the Agency to proceed with the imple -

--- Document Chunk 4826 ---
mentation of the Strengthening Plan. 

--- Document Chunk 4827 ---
A very important challenge is represented by the fact that the additional TA allocation needs to be fully covered under 

--- Document Chunk 4828 ---
the existing subsidy envelope. To make best use of this TA allocation and considering the external constraints related to 

--- Document Chunk 4829 ---
the indexation of salaries and prices, the Agency is making a thorough assessment of its capacity to cover these costs in 

--- Document Chunk 4830 ---
a sustainable manner until the end of MFF 2021-2027. Several measures are envisaged, such as the time-phased hiring of 

--- Document Chunk 4831 ---
the TAs. The budget constraint on the subsidy side is therefore an element to be properly monitored and managed for the 

--- Document Chunk 4832 ---
whole remaining period of the current MFF. 

--- Document Chunk 4833 ---
The current document describes the plan of actions which the Agency will put in place in the period 2023-2027 in order 

--- Document Chunk 4834 ---
to implement the Strengthening Plan, taking into consideration the level of additional staff allocation proposed by the EC. 

--- Document Chunk 4835 ---
It is hereinafter referred as SAP (Strengthening Action Plan) 2023-2027. This builds on actions already taken up to present 

--- Document Chunk 4836 ---
to increase the efficiency of the support services and tools.

--- Document Chunk 4837 ---
A�2� W hat we want to achieve

--- Document Chunk 4838 ---
ERA has established an outcome-driven framework, placing strong emphasis on effectiveness (i.e. “doing the right things”), 

--- Document Chunk 4839 ---
in line with the prioritisation of activities included in the Strengthening Plan. In parallel, a delivery structure based on pro-

--- Document Chunk 4840 ---
grammes has been established. Outputs of programmes are followed up and measured using a dashboard approach.

--- Document Chunk 4841 ---
With the Strengthening Plan, we will implement a series of improvement actions that should enable to achieve the most 

--- Document Chunk 4842 ---
appropriate outcomes with the resources available. This is important not only to justify the additional resources requested 

--- Document Chunk 4843 ---
by the Agency, but also in order to demonstrate that European taxpayer’s money is used in the most effective way, so that 

--- Document Chunk 4844 ---
the European railway system can develop towards attractiveness, efficiency, and sustainability.

--- Document Chunk 4845 ---
Improvement actions will be assessed according to their impact as well as ease of implementation. Quantitative targets 

--- Document Chunk 4846 ---
are defined (mainly related to the respective FTEs) and followed up/measured on a regular basis. The baseline is ERA SPD 

--- Document Chunk 4847 ---
2022, and the monitoring tools are ERA SPD Portfolio Management together with the SPD Dashboard developed already.

--- Document Chunk 4848 ---
A�3� Objec tives, actions, indicators, and targets

--- Document Chunk 4849 ---
The SAP 2023-2027 mirrors the Strengthening Plan and translated it into concrete actions. It is based on the planning 

--- Document Chunk 4850 ---
and monitoring framework and enablers already set up by the Agency, which includes: 

--- Document Chunk 4851 ---
 − the multi-annual planning in the SPD, with a clear focus on the intervention logic; 

--- Document Chunk 4852 ---
 − the Agency’s performance dashboard, including reporting to the EB and the MB

--- Document Chunk 4853 ---
 − the regular budget execution monitoring and reporting

--- Document Chunk 4854 ---
 − the Consolidated Annual Activity Report.

--- Document Chunk 4855 ---

The annual work programmes will therefore be aligned to the priorities listed in the SAP ,

which represents an anchor for the multi-annual planning in what the priority policy areas

are concerned. A direct tracking of SAP-related FTEs, outputs and targets will be includes

in the SPDs.

The SAP 2023-2027 is organised along the following components/objectives:

puts and outcomes, including efficiency gains

--- Document Chunk 4866 ---
regularity and legality

--- Document Chunk 4867 ---
d)  Ensure the overall projected FTE evolution by 2027

e)  Ensure effective and efficient budget management (planning and execution), ap -

--- Document Chunk 4869 ---
propriate risk management

A.3.3. Ensure a re duction in the Agency’s administrative FTE allocation

--- Document Chunk 5413 ---
Note 1: This objective is referred to the administrative FTE allocation but encompasses a wide scope (e.g. redeploying administrative posts to operational activities, redeploying technical staff who 

--- Document Chunk 5414 ---
currently cover administrative tasks to operational tasks activities).

--- Document Chunk 5415 ---
All references are to FTEs (not posts) to allow for counting savings and/or redeployments which account for partitions of one FTE.

--- Document Chunk 5416 ---
Note 2: The sequencing is thought as follows: 

--- Document Chunk 5417 ---
i.  Creating the capacity of potentially free FTEs through process leaning, including automation – as such, this does not account for a materialised saving, but is a pre-condition (step 

--- Document Chunk 5418 ---
C2)

--- Document Chunk 5419 ---
ii.  Identifying the opportunities to materialise that capacity – this can happen at contract end points (step C3)

--- Document Chunk 5420 ---
iii.  Having the FTEs freed from administrative work needs to be followed up by their actual redeployment in operational areas (step C4)

--- Document Chunk 5421 ---
(96) T his reflects the re-visited assumptions for the use of ERA FTEs for VA, SSC, ERTMS TA compared to 2022 and also embeds a component of efficiency gains through simplification/automation of processes.

--- Document Chunk 5623 ---
Budget related

--- Document Chunk 5624 ---
Risk Risk assessment Mitigating measures

--- Document Chunk 5625 ---
1. The Agency might not be in the position to hire all 12 TAs in 2023 due to subsidy constraints. The 

--- Document Chunk 5626 ---
inflation trend poses significant pressure on the Agency’s capacity to cover the salary costs in the 

--- Document Chunk 5627 ---
absence of sufficient additional EU subsidy.

--- Document Chunk 5628 ---
4

--- Document Chunk 5629 ---
The Agency is carefully monitoring the budget execution to strike the 

--- Document Chunk 5630 ---
optimal use of the existing resources in the spirit of sound financial 

--- Document Chunk 5631 ---
management, while flagging early warning signals in case of subsidy 

--- Document Chunk 5632 ---
gaps. We will react by an agile approach, having reserve lists in place 

--- Document Chunk 5633 ---
but only conclude employment contracts when the budgetary means 

--- Document Chunk 5634 ---
are available.

--- Document Chunk 5635 ---
2. The revenues from Fees and Charges are not under the full control of the Agency. In particular, 

--- Document Chunk 5636 ---
the volume of work can fluctuate due to seasonal trends during the year, but also more structurally, 

--- Document Chunk 5637 ---
upwards (e.g. the need for re-certification following DAC deployment, go-everywhere trains etc.) or 

--- Document Chunk 5638 ---
downwards (e.g. starting with the second round of safety certification for the same RU at ERA, the 

--- Document Chunk 5639 ---
complexity of the issues and checks might drop compared to the first round).

--- Document Chunk 5640 ---
4

--- Document Chunk 5641 ---
Human resources and internal communication related

--- Document Chunk 5642 ---
Risk Risk assessment Mitigating measures

--- Document Chunk 5643 ---
3. The changes in the working patterns, together with the financial consideration for hiring at lower 

--- Document Chunk 5644 ---
grades, might limit the attractiveness for the specialised technical jobs offered by the Agency in 

--- Document Chunk 5645 ---
the future. This might hamper the business continuity, talent pool retention and by consequence, 

--- Document Chunk 5646 ---
Agency’s capacity to deliver the technical outputs envisaged in this plan.

--- Document Chunk 5647 ---
3

--- Document Chunk 5648 ---
4. Inherent internal communication sensitivity around the choices made as part of the action plan 

--- Document Chunk 5649 ---
(non-replacement, redeployment etc.). In addition, given this internal redeployment, the pressure on 

--- Document Chunk 5650 ---
legally binding administrative tasks will increase exponentially. 

--- Document Chunk 5651 ---
4

--- Document Chunk 5652 ---
The Agency will indeed tackle this aspect with attention, by 

--- Document Chunk 5653 ---
highlighting and supporting the opportunity of ensuring career paths 

--- Document Chunk 5654 ---
from administrative tasks to operational tasks. Natural end-of-contract 

--- Document Chunk 5655 ---
gate reviews will be used.

--- Document Chunk 5656 ---
Output related

--- Document Chunk 5657 ---
Risk Risk assessment Mitigating measures

--- Document Chunk 5658 ---
5. With insufficient additional resources for the policy tasks, up to the full level of the need, the 

--- Document Chunk 5659 ---
Agency might not be in the position to support the EC in responding to all standardisation areas 

--- Document Chunk 5660 ---
linked to innovation over the next years. The allocation of additional resources might need to be 

--- Document Chunk 5661 ---
reopened during the lifecycle of this Action Plan to identify priority areas for which the Agency’s 

--- Document Chunk 5662 ---
involvement is further expected.

--- Document Chunk 5663 ---
3

--- Document Chunk 5664 ---
6. Considering the complexity of the training program which could help redeploying administrative 

--- Document Chunk 5665 ---
staff to operational tasks, it might have a limited buy in and/or efficiency and could require a period 

--- Document Chunk 5666 ---
of time for completion which goes beyond the timeline of the Strengthening Plan.

--- Document Chunk 5667 ---
